<div class=\"widget widget-ArticleFulltext widget-instance-OUP_Article_FullText_Widget\">\n        <div class=\"module-widget\">\r\n    <div class=\"widget-items\" data-widgetname=\"ArticleFulltext\">\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n                    <h2 scrollto-destination=109886454 id=\"109886454\" class=\"abstract-title\" >Abstract</h2>\r\n<section class=\"abstract\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">We report on discovery results from a quasar lens search in the ATLAS-DR3 public footprint. Spectroscopic follow-up campaigns, conducted at the 2.6 m Nordic Optical Telescope (La Palma) and 3.6\u00a0m New Technology Telescope (La Silla) in 2016, yielded seven pairs of quasars exhibiting the same lines at the same redshift and monotonic flux ratios with wavelength (hereafter NIQs, nearly identical quasar pairs). Magellan spectra of A0140\u22121152 (01<sup>h</sup>40<sup>m</sup>03<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${^{\\rm s}_{.}}$|</span>0\u201311<sup>d</sup>52<sup>m</sup>19<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${^{\\rm s}_{.}}$|</span>0, <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.807) confirm it as a lens with deflector at <em>z</em><sub>l</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.277 and Einstein radius \u03b8<sub>E</sub>\u00a0=\u00a0(0.73\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.02)\u2009arcsec. Follow-up imaging of the NIQ A2213\u22122652 (22<sup>h</sup>13<sup>m</sup>38<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${^{\\rm s}_{.}}$|</span>4\u201326<sup>d</sup>52<sup>m</sup>27<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${^{\\rm s}_{.}}$|</span>1) reveals the deflector galaxy and confirms it as a lens. We show the use of spatial resolution from the <em>Gaia</em> mission to select lenses and list additional systems from a WISE-<em>Gaia</em>-ATLAS search, yielding three additional lenses (02<sup>h</sup>35<sup>m</sup>27<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${^{\\rm s}_{.}}$|</span>4\u201324<sup>d</sup>33<sup>m</sup>13<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${^{\\rm s}_{.}}$|</span>2, 02<sup>h</sup>59<sup>m</sup>33<sup>s</sup>\u201323<sup>d</sup>38<sup>m</sup>01<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${^{\\rm s}_{.}}$|</span>8, 01<sup>h</sup>46<sup>m</sup>32<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${^{\\rm s}_{.}}$|</span>9\u201311<sup>d</sup>33<sup>m</sup>39<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${^{\\rm s}_{.}}$|</span>0). The overall sample consists of 11 lenses/NIQs, plus three lenses known before 2016, over the ATLAS-DR3 footprint (\u22483500\u2009deg<sup>2</sup>). Finally, we discuss future prospects for objective classification of pair/NIQ/contaminant spectra.</p></section>                        <div class=\"article-metadata-panel clearfix\"></div>\r\n<div class=\"kwd-group\"><a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;gravitational lensing: strong&quot;\">gravitational lensing: strong</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;methods: statistical&quot;\">methods: statistical</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;techniques: image processing&quot;\">techniques: image processing</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"surveys\">surveys</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;quasars: general&quot;\">quasars: general</a></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=109886456 id=\"109886456\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec1>1 INTRODUCTION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">In an era of large data stemming from ever more ambitious surveys, large samples of intrinsically rare objects become possible. Quasar pairs and strongly lensed quasars are particularly interesting classes of rare astronomical objects, because the information content for each system is high and in some sense unique. Through the lensing effect, one can obtain<sup><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn1\" data-open=\"fn1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\">1</a></sup> (i) a purely gravitational measurement of the properties of the deflector(s), including their invisible components like dark matter haloes and individual stars (e.g. Oguri, Rusu &amp; Falco <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib28\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib28\" data-open=\"bib28\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>); (ii) a magnified view of the background quasar, accretion disc, and host galaxy (Peng et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib29\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib29\" data-open=\"bib29\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>; Sluse et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib40\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib40\" data-open=\"bib40\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>; Ding et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib12\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib12\" data-open=\"bib12\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>; Motta et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib24\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib24\" data-open=\"bib24\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>); (iii) information about distances and thus cosmological parameters (Refsdal <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib31\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib31\" data-open=\"bib31\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1964</a>; C\u00e1rdenas et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>; Treu &amp; Marshall <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib45\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib45\" data-open=\"bib45\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>; Suyu et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib43\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib43\" data-open=\"bib43\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>). Spectroscopy of close sightlines, be they to multiple quasar images or to pairs of physically distinct quasars, is a probe of (i) kinematics of the cosmic web at high redshift (Rauch et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib30\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib30\" data-open=\"bib30\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2005</a>); (ii) small-scale structure of Ly\u2009\u03b1 absorbers (Smette et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib41\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib41\" data-open=\"bib41\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1992</a>; Dinshaw et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib13\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib13\" data-open=\"bib13\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1998</a>; Rorai et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib32\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib32\" data-open=\"bib32\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>); (iii) physical conditions of the cool ISM/CGM of galaxies and quasars (Farina et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>; Zahedy et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib50\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib50\" data-open=\"bib50\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Unfortunately, lensed quasars are rare on the sky \u2013 typically 1 per 10 square degrees (deg<sup>2</sup>) at depth and resolution of present day surveys (Oguri &amp; Marshall <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib26\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib26\" data-open=\"bib26\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>) \u2013 since they require a very close alignment of quasars with foreground massive galaxies, or galaxy clusters. Finding them is thus a classic needle in a haystack problem, that requires sophisticated algorithms to identify promising candidates for further follow-up and confirmation. In the case of current wide field imaging surveys consisting of thousands of <em>deg</em><sup>2</sup>, the data mining problem consists of identifying of order \u223c100 candidates from catalogues consisting of 10<sup>7</sup>\u201310<sup>8</sup> astronomical sources.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">In imaging surveys, lensed quasars can be recognized from their colours and morphology. In photometric catalogues, they can appear as quasars with contributions from the lensing galaxy, or galaxies with contributions from the background source, or anything intermediate. Their image cutouts have morphologies that may be more or less marked, ranging from wide-separation lenses with a clearly visible deflector, to lenses whose image-separation can be ascertained just by direct modelling of the cutouts. In order to ensure maximum efficiency and purity, search strategies have typically been tailored to the specifics of each survey in the past. Partially overlapping areas of the Southern hemisphere are being probed in (at least) <em>griz</em> bands by the DES (S\u00e1nchez &amp; DES Collaboration <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib33\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib33\" data-open=\"bib33\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>; Dark Energy Survey Collaboration <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib10\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib10\" data-open=\"bib10\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>), KiDS (de Jong et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib11\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib11\" data-open=\"bib11\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>), Pan-STARRS (Chambers et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib8\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib8\" data-open=\"bib8\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>), and VST-ATLAS (Shanks et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib36\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib36\" data-open=\"bib36\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>). The typical resolution of these surveys is just below 1\u2009arcsec full width at half-maximum (FWHM), in most cases insufficient to fully deblend the multiple images and the deflector for galaxy-scale lenses, at least at pipeline and object-detection level.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Therefore, follow-up is almost always necessary, consisting of spectroscopy to confirm that the quasars are indeed multiply imaged and not a chance alignment, and possibly detect spectral features from the deflector, and high-resolution images to map out the lensing configuration. Sometimes confirmation is pretty straightforward, other times it requires substantial observational resources, including <em>Hubble Space Telescope</em> imaging. For example, veritable lenses, like HE1104 (Wisotzki et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib48\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib48\" data-open=\"bib48\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1993</a>) or HS2209 (Hagen, Engels &amp; Reimers <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib16\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib16\" data-open=\"bib16\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1999</a>), were identified as \u2018bright\u2019 quasar pairs with almost identical spectra and had to wait for deeper and high-resolution follow-up (e.g. Chantry, Sluse &amp; Magain <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib9\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib9\" data-open=\"bib9\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>) for a full confirmation. Others (e.g. the quad WFI 2026, Morgan et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib23\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib23\" data-open=\"bib23\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2004</a>) are lacking secure spectroscopy of the deflector to this day. These systems are not uncommon in quasar lens searches: the Sloan Quasar Lens Search (SQLS: Oguri et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib27\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib27\" data-open=\"bib27\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>; Inada et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib18\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib18\" data-open=\"bib18\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>; More et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib22\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib22\" data-open=\"bib22\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>) yielded some quasar pairs with nearly identical spectra at the same redshifts, but not deflectors detected. In small separation lenses, the deflector may be faint enough to be undetectable unless the quasar images are subtracted from deep, high-resolution imaging data (e.g. for HS2209, Williams et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib47\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib47\" data-open=\"bib47\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017b</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Here, we report on spectroscopic follow-up results from a two-step search applied mainly to the VST-ATLAS public footprint.<sup><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn2\" data-open=\"fn2\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\">2</a></sup> In Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec2\"></span><a href=\"#sec2\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">2</a>, we describe the <em>target</em> and <em>candidate</em> selection procedures; follow-up campaigns are summarized in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec3\"></span><a href=\"#sec3\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">3</a>; results are discussed in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec4\"></span><a href=\"#sec4\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">4</a> and Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>; we discuss future prospects in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec5\"></span><a href=\"#sec5\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">5</a>, and list additional candidates (Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl4\" data-open=\"tbl4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a>) that could not be followed up in 2016, including the first quasar lens candidates identified using <em>Gaia</em> data and three new lenses among them. Target selection was based on <em>g, r, i, z</em> and WISE (Wright et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib49\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib49\" data-open=\"bib49\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>) <em>W</em>1, <em>W</em>2 magnitudes. For consistency with previous work, the WISE magnitudes were left in the Vega system, whereas the ATLAS magnitudes were translated in the AB system.</p>                        <a id=\"109886462\" scrollto-destination=\"109886462\"></a>\r\n<div content-id=\"tbl1\" class=\"table-modal table-full-width-wrap\"><div class=\"table-wrap table-wide\"><div class=\"table-wrap-title\" id=\"tbl1\" data-id=\"tbl1\"><span class=\"label\">Table 1.</span><div class=\"caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Model-accepted candidates from ATLAS DR2 (first sub-list), SDSS control set (second sub-list), and ATLAS-DR3 (third sub-list) targets, that were observed with long-slit spectroscopy at NOT and NTT over 2016. target=\"_blank\" href=\"/view-large/109886462\">\r\n          Open in new tab\r\n        </a></div></div></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=109886463 id=\"109886463\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2>2 TARGETS AND CANDIDATES</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The strategy followed here consists of two steps. First, <em>targets</em> are selected from the ATLAS catalogues based on their magnitudes in optical and infra-red magnitudes. Then, <em>candidates</em> are obtained by retaining just the targets that pass a first visual inspection and modelling their cutouts, to ensure that they are consistent with two or more point-sources with consistent colours. A similar search was performed on a patch of the SDSS footprint with right ascensions accessible to observation around February 2016, further concentrating on four objects with SDSS fibre spectra that were used as a control sample.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">A different kind of target mining, based on outlier selection (Agnello <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>), was applied to the ATLAS-DR3 footprint once it became publicly available in November 2016. For the ATLAS-DR3 and SDSS targets, the only candidate selection step consisted in visual inspection.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=109886466 id=\"109886466\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-1>2.1  ATLAS DR2 target selection</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The coverage of ATLAS over its footprint is not uniform in all bands. Then, different selection procedures were adopted for different combinations of bands, in order to maximize the target sample. When querying objects from the ATLAS public footprint, we required an extendedness criterion, given by either <span class=\"monospace\">p_Galaxy</span>&gt;0.5 or <span class=\"monospace\">AperMag3_i-AperMag6_i</span>&gt;0.08, i.e. that the objects have extra flux besides that of an isolated point-source.</p>                    <h4 scrollto-destination=109886468 id=\"109886468\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-1-1>2.1.1 Artificial Neural Networks</h4>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">When <em>griz</em> bands were available, we selected objects that are \u2018blue and extended\u2019, using colour cuts along the lines of Agnello et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015b</a>), but without restrictions on <em>i</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>W</em>2 or <em>g</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>i</em>. This is to avoid the exclusion of higher redshift quasars (<em>z</em><sub>s</sub> \u2273 2) and redder objects where a lensing galaxy could contribute more to the colours. For these objects, we used Artificial Neural Networks (ANNs) to select those that were compatible with lensed quasars, or quasars at redshift <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0&gt;\u00a00.75; this was made possible by extending the ANNs designed by Agnello et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib2\" data-open=\"bib2\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015a</a>) to split the \u2018quasar\u2019 class into multiple redshift intervals (cf. Williams, Agnello &amp; Treu <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib46\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib46\" data-open=\"bib46\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>), bringing the total number of classes to nine from the initial four that were used by Agnello et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015b</a>).</p>                    <h4 scrollto-destination=109886470 id=\"109886470\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-1-2>2.1.2 Missing magnitudes and hybrid colours</h4>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">In the absence of some optical bands, we could still select some objects based on their infra-red excess, i.e. optical colours resembling those of quasars and redder optical-infrared colours that could be indicative of a lensing galaxy. This approach was used successfully by Ofek et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib25\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib25\" data-open=\"bib25\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2007</a>) in the case of the SDSS, and we used it here with either <em>g</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>r</em> or <em>r</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>z</em> for the optical colours and <em>r</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>H</em> or <em>r</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>K</em><sub>s</sub> for the hybrid colours, whenever <em>H</em> or <em>K</em><sub>s</sub> magnitudes are available from 2MASS (Skrutskie et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib37\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib37\" data-open=\"bib37\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>).</p><div class=\"&#xA;            block-child-p&#xA;            \">An additional sub-sample of targets consisted of objects that satisfied some strict colour\u2013magnitude cuts <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equ1\" content-id=\"equ1\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{eqnarray}\r\ni-W1&lt;3.7,\\ \\ g-i&lt;0.65,\\nonumber \\\\\r\n\\ W1-W2&gt;1.075,\\ W2&lt;13.4.\r\n\\end{eqnarray} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(1)</span></div>This identifies the locus where 7 out of the 10 small-separation lenses of Inada et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib18\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib18\" data-open=\"bib18\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>) lie. They are dominated by the source quasar, being blue in the optical and having a high WISE excess, and a low <em>i</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>W</em>1 typical of quasars at higher redshift.</div>                    <h4 scrollto-destination=109886473 id=\"109886473\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-1-3>2.1.3 Colour grading of DR2 targets</h4>\r\n<div class=\"&#xA;            block-child-p&#xA;            \">Targets in the ATLAS DR2 footprint were also graded based on their colours, where a grade of 0 (resp. 3) means low (resp. high) chances to be a quasar lens. The colour grade was assigned as <em>s</em>\u00a0=\u00a01\u00a0+\u00a0<em>s</em><sub>1</sub>\u00a0+\u00a0<em>s</em><sub>2</sub>\u00a0+\u00a0<em>s</em><sub>3</sub>\u00a0+\u00a0<em>s</em><sub>4</sub>, with <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equ2\" content-id=\"equ2\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{eqnarray}\r\ns_{1}&amp;=&amp;\\theta (-0.5(g-r+0.8(u-g-0.6)-0.4))\\nonumber \\\\\r\ns_{2}&amp;=&amp;0.5H(3.6-(W2-W3))-0.5H(W2-W3-3.6)\\nonumber \\\\\r\ns_{3}&amp;=&amp;0.5H(3.1+1.5(W1-W2-1.075)-(W2-W3))\\nonumber \\\\\r\ns_{4}&amp;=&amp;0.5H(3.4-(i-W1)),\r\n\\end{eqnarray} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(2)</span></div>where the Heaviside step function <em>H</em>(<em>x</em>) is 1 (resp. 0) for <em>x</em>\u00a0&gt;\u00a00 (resp. <em>x</em>\u00a0&lt;\u00a00), and \u03b8(<em>x</em>)\u00a0=\u00a0<em>x</em> for \u22120.5\u00a0&lt;\u00a0<em>x</em>\u00a0&lt;\u00a00.5 and \u03b8(<em>x</em>)\u00a0=\u00a00.5 (resp. \u22120.5) for <em>x</em>\u00a0&gt;\u00a00.5 (resp. &lt;\u22120.5). Whenever a magnitude is not available (especially <em>u</em>), the grade to which it contributes is set to 0.</div>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=109886475 id=\"109886475\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-2>2.2 Candidate selection</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">From the previous step, we obtained a pool of targets that were further refined to obtain a final candidate sample. First, the targets were visually inspected by three of us (AA, TT, CER) to exclude obvious contaminants, such as galaxies, low-redshift quasars with a bright host, line-of-sight quasar-galaxy alignments, isolated objects and pairs with colours that were manifestly inconsistent. As a second step, the multiband ATLAS-DR2 cutouts were modelled automatically to verify whether the objects could be \u2018split\u2019 into two (or more) point-sources with consistent colours across the available magnitudes, as described below.</p>                    <h4 scrollto-destination=109886477 id=\"109886477\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-2-1>2.2.1 Candidate corroboration</h4>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Fourteen of the 15 DR1 and DR2 candidates for which spectra were eventually obtained were independently evaluated as candidates using the ATLAS cutout morphology approach described by Schechter et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib35\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib35\" data-open=\"bib35\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>). Of these, 10 had been independently targeted by them for cutout evaluation based solely on a simple cut on the <em>W</em>1\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>W</em>2 colour.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Besides accepting or rejecting a target, this procedure also assigned grades corresponding to different diagnostics (see Schechter et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib35\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib35\" data-open=\"bib35\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>, for details). For the sake of completeness, we retain the <span class=\"monospace\">ufom</span> overall figure of merit in what follows, even though it was not used to prioritize candidates for follow-up.</p>                    <h4 scrollto-destination=109886480 id=\"109886480\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-2-2>2.2.2 General candidate properties</h4>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The cutout-modelling stage enabled a further refinement of the visual-inspection survivors into model-accepted and model-rejected candidates. Their selected colour\u2013magnitude diagrams are displayed in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>. The histograms of colour-grade of the model-accepted and rejected targets are shown in the bottom panel. Between half and two thirds of the DR2 targets with grade &gt;2 are accepted by the cutout modelling.</p>                        <a id=\"109886482\" scrollto-destination=\"109886482\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig1\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 1.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/475/2/10.1093_mnras_stx3226/1/m_stx3226fig1.jpeg?Expires=1611466225&amp;Signature=vy6gRpUzprMEM~-tP-NlzKS1JC1LOP3QVgUcoCaDwJzNIG2y2Q7ywVsUqMx0-I0bjSjsm5LvNV0-tSuU~tJDXK8tjT~xoZuajK5WuFsnD29LdDpN2XV2L6h3o9k7afy8Vi~ZolYnxS7pHU0YLbcHx0V~YugCSVaV1hOf4VsXSb338teh3802b4nWjVNGE-aPtzqmi8vHj4zYyB0Lbg6MUqTnZh6UXPpWFTtKqavNfFHHLBbW0CzRPkaGaT8Ojg8vK-gFDpx1Rfjt0tIR0mQ3-Lr~oPMJ1b7Y2-mmWN5WljJesVvc3tk4kNW8xDaaGLUOmmP4HnSEWHdvc9T08iCFDA__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Colour\u2013magnitude diagrams of ANN and IRX targets that passed a first round of visual inspection. The red (resp. black) points indicate candidates that were accepted (resp. rejected) by the model selection of Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec2-2\"></span><a href=\"#sec2-2\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">2.2</a>. The dashed lines represent the Assef et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib5\" data-open=\"bib5\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>) locus (top-left panel), the detection limit <em>W</em>3\u00a0=\u00a011.6 (middle-left panel), a rough separation of high-<em>z</em> quasars from lower-<em>z</em> quasars and early-type galaxies (top-right) and galaxy-like and lens-like objects (middle-right). The bottom panel shows the colour-grade histograms of model-accepted (resp. rejected) candidates in red (resp. black dashed).</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">From the colour\u2013magnitude diagrams, model-rejected targets tend to lie at lower <em>W</em>1\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>W</em>2 or higher <em>W</em>2\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>W</em>3, which are regions typically populated by galaxies or, at best, quasars with an extended host. The dashed lines in <em>W</em>1\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>W</em>2 versus <em>W</em>2\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>W</em>3 separate most of the model-accepted candidates from the rest, with different thresholds. The upper line also happens to separate the 10 SQLS small separation lenses of Inada et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib18\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib18\" data-open=\"bib18\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>) from about half of the 40 false-positives in that search. This suggests that <em>W</em>2\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>W</em>3 adds information over the original ANN implementation (see in particular Williams, Agnello &amp; Treu <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib46\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib46\" data-open=\"bib46\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>, for a detailed discussion), and in fact this is used in the outlier selection method (Agnello <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>) that has been applied to the DR3 data.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=109886484 id=\"109886484\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec3>3 FOLLOW-UP</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Long-slit spectroscopy was used to ascertain the nature of the candidates. The DR2 and SDSS candidates were mostly observed with the Andalucia Faint Object Spectrograph and Camera (ALFOSC) at the 2.6\u00a0m Nordic Optical Telescope (NOT) in La Palma (Spain). The remaining candidates from DR2 and DR3 were observed with the ESO Faint Object Spectrograph and Camera (EFOSC2) at the 3.6\u00a0m New Technology Telescope (NTT) in La Silla (Chile). The objects are listed in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">For one object, A0140\u22121152, we also show spectra taken with <span class=\"small-caps\">imacs</span> at the 6.5m Walter Baade Telescope at Magellan (Las Campanas), where a red galaxy at <em>z</em><sub>l</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.277 is detected between two quasar images at <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.807, making this system most likely a lens. This system was observed on <span class=\"small-caps\">ut</span> 2016 November 28, IMACS was set up in \u2018long\u2019 <em>f</em>/4 camera mode, and a 3800\u20137000\u2009\u212b filter was used.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Custom routines were used for data reduction, as specified below for the two setups. The sky subtraction and 1D spectral extraction were performed in a second stage, on the reduced 2D spectra (Agnello et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015b</a>; Schechter et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib35\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib35\" data-open=\"bib35\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>). At each wavelength pixel, the raw data in the spatial direction were modelled as a superposition of two (or more) Gaussians and a spatially uniform component for the sky lines. Within each science frame, the Gaussians are forced to have the same FWHM and the same separation across the whole wavelength range, even though their peak positions are allowed to vary (linearly) with wavelength. The extracted 1D spectra of each component were then co-added, and data and noise spectra were obtained via de-trended fluctuation analysis, with a 5+5 wavelength-pixel window and a quadratic polynomial for the de-trending. This procedure allowed us to reliably separate the multiple components in all observed candidates despite sub-optimal observing conditions, with seeing FWHM between \u22481 and 1.5\u2009arcsec and clouds during the NOT observations, and variable weather and seeing during the NTT observations.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=109886488 id=\"109886488\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec3-1>3.1 NOT follow-up</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The data were obtained on 2016 February 5 and 6 as part of a Niels Bohr Institute Guaranteed Time Observing Program (P52-802). We positioned 1-arcsec-wide long slits through the candidate multiple images and used ALFOSC with the #4 grism, covering the wavelength range <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$3200\\,\\rm {^{\\circ}_{\\rm A}} &lt;\\lambda &lt; 9600\\,\\rm {^{\\circ}_{\\rm A}}$|</span> with a dispersion of <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$3.3\\,\\rm {^{\\circ}_{\\rm A}}\\,\\rm {pixel}^{-1}$|\u2060</span>. Two science exposures were taken per object, with arc (HeNe, Ar) and flat lamps bracketing each observing block. Standard <span class=\"small-caps\">iraf</span> routines were used for bias subtraction, flat-field corrections and wavelength solution.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=109886490 id=\"109886490\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec3-2>3.2 NTT follow-up</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The data were obtained on 2016 September 25\u201327 and 2016 December 5 at the ESO-NTT (PI Anguita, 097.A-0473(A), 098.A-0395(A)). The 1.2-arcsec-wide long slit in combination with EFOSC grism #13 was used, covering <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$3400\\,\\rm {^{\\circ}_{\\rm A}} &lt;\\lambda &lt;10\\,000\\,\\rm {^{\\circ}_{\\rm A}}$|</span> with <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${\\approx }5.5\\,\\rm {^{\\circ}_{\\rm A}}\\,\\rm {pixel}^{-1}$|\u2060</span>. Mostly one exposure was taken per object, with calibrations taken once per night. The ESO-provided pipeline (v2.5.5) was used for data reduction.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=109886492 id=\"109886492\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4>4 DISCUSSION AND CONCLUSIONS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Long-slit spectra of 27 objects were obtained (Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>), out of which seven were <em>nearly identical quasar pairs</em> (NIQs), i.e. pairs of quasars with the same lines at the same redshift and smooth flux ratios as measured on the continua. These could be veritable lenses where the deflector has not been detected yet, or truly physical pairs of quasars. At least one of them, A0140\u22121152, is a lens based on the deeper Magellan spectra (Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig4\" data-open=\"fig4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a>). An eighth system, A1020\u22121002, is a pair of quasars at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a02.03 (Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig6\" data-open=\"fig6\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">6</a>) and could also be an NIQ, with flux ratio <em>f</em><sub>r</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.3 measured between C <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] and Mg <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>, but deeper data are needed. Some, peculiar false positives are discussed in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec4-2\"></span><a href=\"#sec4-2\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">4.2</a>.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=109886494 id=\"109886494\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4-1>4.1 Near-identical quasar pairs</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Seven objects have two quasar spectra with the same lines at the same redshift and same shapes, and monotonic flux ratios as measured on the continua (Figs\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a> \u2013<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig4\" data-open=\"fig4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a>). Four, marked by asterisks in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>, were also flagged independently in the search described by Schechter et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib35\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib35\" data-open=\"bib35\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>, whence the terminology of NIQs is adopted). In all cases the traces could be reliably deconvolved, and their flux ratios vary from \u22481 to \u224810 for the sample. One NIQ was found among the four SDSS targets with quasar fibre spectra, the others being quasar+quasar or quasar+star alignments. Two lenses, A1012\u22120307 and A0140\u22121152, are described in the following sections. Follow-up imaging of the NIQ A2213\u22122652, from a subsequent campaign (Keck-NIRC2, 2017 October, PI Treu; not shown here), reveal the deflector between the two quasar components, confirming this system as a third lens.</p>                        <a id=\"109886496\" scrollto-destination=\"109886496\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig2\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 2.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/475/2/10.1093_mnras_stx3226/1/m_stx3226fig2.jpeg?Expires=1611466225&amp;Signature=eTvqRvBqUwWCFTtQ~3hqnpR0ucbfN6tB1dcHkJDJuarrBwE53Ioj6Hq-9j77sMlq1kaRdOGS9XdZnSIHBFJJqk0-wp2pjuwlOnCob3uBv9eDBwgNyoZUqO2~p~DSwmfjK5A4RhX5mkpnxgQGDSB9NFU-~MyUMvYUolng7LPUK0k4CmxjH1G0IUPJpphelJYL7yA4~nm7ukBzhnG-BDYh8Uj3ICV~sVZr1czejfM-gUrM4pQm0DfMiKUq4vPIAIHwWV49m5snUeN9TLkkBjqqo7~1BV1WnxKQUztH6KTX8qZ7I6oq5k3xC1p0G56UryK8gdjwvLfNe-wwKndcRrf9nQ__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Deconvolved long-slit spectra of six NIQs (see Table\u00a01). <em>Bottom right:</em> same model, but only the quasar images are subtracted.</p></div></div>                    <h4 scrollto-destination=109886499 id=\"109886499\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4-1-1>4.1.1 A1012-0307, a known lens with power-law flux ratios</h4>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">A1012\u22120307 is the known lens LBQS1009\u22120252 (Hewett et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib17\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib17\" data-open=\"bib17\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1994</a>). The NTT data can be well deblended into two <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.745 quasar spectra, showing the same lines with the same shape (Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>). The redshift from NTT spectra is slightly higher than the one (<em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.739) quoted in its original discovery paper. Differently from the other NIQs, whose flux ratios are almost constant with wavelength, in this case the flux ratio is well fitted over the whole spectral range by <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$f_{\\text{r}}=3.0(\\lambda /9000\\,\\rm {^{\\circ}_{\\rm A}})^{-1}.$|</span> In principle, such a variation could be produced by intrinsically different continua in two physically separate quasars, or significant differential reddening by a foreground galaxy. In simple models of doubly imaged quasars (without shear), the fainter image forms closer to the lens and so can be more heavily reddened. Still within the lensing hypothesis, also microlensing should be considered as a possible source of chromatic flux ratios.</p>                    <h4 scrollto-destination=109886501 id=\"109886501\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4-1-2>4.1.2 A0140\u22121152, a new quasar lens</h4>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">A0140 was observed at the NTT and Magellan independently (Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig4\" data-open=\"fig4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a>), having been respectively targeted in the ATLAS-DR3 catalogue and separately found via cutout modelling in the whole footprint. Both data sets revealed <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.806\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.001 nearly-identical quasar spectra, plus a red \u2018excess\u2019 between the two traces that the Magellan spectra and acquisition images confirmed to be a galaxy at <em>z</em><sub>l</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.277 with prominent Ca (G, H, K) absorption features. The flux ratio between the two quasar images, as measured on the continua, is <em>f</em><sub>r</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.05 between C lines on the blue side and <em>f</em><sub>r</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.12 on the red side; the NTT spectra gave <em>f</em><sub>r</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.2 between the C <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>]/Fe complex and Mg <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>. The small discrepancy may be ascribed to lower S/N, atmospheric dispersion corrections and slight slit misalignment.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">For this system, we also run simple lens models. From the IMACS <em>i</em>-band acquisition image, aligned with the slit (Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig4\" data-open=\"fig4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a>), the relative positions and magnitudes of the quasar images and deflector have been obtained, as listed in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl2\" data-open=\"tbl2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>. The flux ratio between images A and B varies depending on whether it is measured on the continua or on (continuum-subtracted) emission lines, or on the broad-band IMACS image. Besides instrumental effects (chromatic atmospheric refraction and slit-losses), this chromaticity results from differential extinction in the deflector and microlensing. We then adopt <em>f</em><sub>A</sub>/<em>f</em><sub>B</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.20\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.05 as a measured flux-ratio constraint, which is obtained on the emission lines and accounts for systematics in continuum-subtraction, differential extinction, and instrumental effects. The observational constraints are then: the positions of images A, B relative to G; and the flux ratio <em>f</em><sub>A</sub>/<em>f</em><sub>B</sub>. An additional constraint is the presence of only two (observed) quasar images.</p>                        <a id=\"109886504\" scrollto-destination=\"109886504\"></a>\r\n<div content-id=\"tbl2\" class=\"table-modal table-full-width-wrap\"><div class=\"table-wrap table-wide\"><div class=\"table-wrap-title\" id=\"tbl2\" data-id=\"tbl2\"><span class=\"label\">Table 2.</span><div class=\"caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Astrometry and magnitudes of the three components in A0140. For lens model purposes, we adopt 0.025\u2009arcsec (i.e. 1\u2009pixel/8) for the uncertainties on positions. The <em>i</em>-band magnitudes are calibrated against a bright star in the field of view (<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">\u2060|$\\text{RA}= 01^{\\text{h}}39^{\\text{m}}37{^{\\rm .\u00a0</span></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>A\u00a0</td><td>0.592\u00a0</td><td>0.199\u00a0</td><td>18.226\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>B\u00a0</td><td>\u22120.804\u00a0</td><td>\u22120.231\u00a0</td><td>18.484\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>G\u00a0</td><td>[     .\u00a0</span></th><th>\u03b4<em>x</em> (arcsec)<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th>\u03b4<em>y</em> (arcsec)<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th>mag_i<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th></tr><tr><th><span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th><span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$=\\ -\\cos (\\mathrm{\\text{D}ec.})\\delta$|</span>RA<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th>\u03b4Dec.<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th><span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>A\u00a0</td><td>0.592\u00a0</td><td>0.199\u00a0</td><td>18.226\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>B\u00a0</td><td>\u22120.804\u00a0</td><td>\u22120.231\u00a0</td><td>18.484\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>G\u00a0</td><td>[ 0.00\u00a0</td><td>0.00 ]\u00a0</td><td>19.253\u00a0</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class=\"&#xA;          graphic-wrap&#xA;          \"><a class=\"fig-view-orig openInAnotherWindow btn js-view-large\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"/view-large/109886504\">\r\n          Open in new tab\r\n        </a></div></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">The deflector (<em>G</em>) is described as a singular isothermal ellipsoid (SIE, Kassiola &amp; Kovner <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib19\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib19\" data-open=\"bib19\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1993</a>), and we consider an external shear component to account for (possible) corrections to the quadrupole, e.g. from additional mass along the line of sight or by deviations from a simple, SIE model. A model with free shear and ellipticity is unconstrained, so we explore three restricted models: mod.(a, SIE) adopts an SIE for the deflector, without external shear; mod.(b, SIS+XS) adopts the spherical limit (<em>q</em> \u21921) for <em>G</em> and includes external shear; mod.(c, SIE+XS) includes external shear, and has <em>G</em> described by an SIE with <em>q</em>\u00a0=\u00a00.5 and p.a. = 28.0\u2009deg (E of N) as inferred from the IMACS image.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">A model with SIE + XS and wider, uniform priors on all parameters is discussed in the Appendix. Since this last model is unconstrained, we use it to characterize the quadrupole degeneracy between shear and ellipticity. To this aim, we adopt unrealistically low positional uncertainties, \u03b4<em>x</em>\u00a0=\u00a0\u03b4<em>y</em>\u00a0=\u00a00.01,\u2009arcsec exploring a \u2018tube\u2019 of solutions.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig5\" data-open=\"fig5\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">5</a> summarizes the lens model results, displaying the Fermat potential contours (dashed) and a set of isophotes in the hypothesis of a circular source, for best-fitting SIE models (b, c). The inferred parameters are listed in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl3\" data-open=\"tbl3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a>. The resulting Einstein radius from (a, b) is \u03b8<sub>E</sub>\u00a0=\u00a0(0.73\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.01)\u2009arcsec, very close to half the A\u2013B image separation, and slightly higher for models with more substantial shear/ellipticity. The axial ratio from mod.(b, SIE) is <em>q</em>\u00a0=\u00a00.96\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.03, significantly rounder than the value suggested by IMACS images. This may mean that either the lens axial ratio from the <span class=\"small-caps\">imacs</span> image is biased (due to the proximity of quasar images, coarse resolution, PSF mismatch), or that the overall quadrupole is small but substantial shear and ellipticity are present.</p>                        <a id=\"109886508\" scrollto-destination=\"109886508\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig5\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 5.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/475/2/10.1093_mnras_stx3226/1/m_stx3226fig5.jpeg?Expires=1611466225&amp;Signature=DtV43zRCksm85RpTWE2nj8vlvwxizAgkXP7XuJiAaj4K3Atsr0q~QjO7C8BRJtwTzfrCEhgcBXeDXbk7WGcdqWB6S580~vSwnhSTPTZwohf7hS9d8fPlFX1D27srBz4oRJp~fP~LyaDJwmLkT1DNQPvSiwG9MGIJJJXKo2zMFDgWm6oxEMFcVA92h4pDVPo8mye8JQxTAtaCHXVCJu-RUbDVW0INBAhO776BzqixPKBdc1huB-iqDUB7QCOQPeXH700gEQ4~AhACGON104aMmgHAX6GCLfYhHsyuALG9GjQL~LtBwNmrmVPha9PSbrHCBLtSKjYUlnQfdxwYOibpwA__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Image-plane lens properties of A0140, from SIE models (left, b; right, c). class=\"&#xA;          graphic-wrap&#xA;          \"><a class=\"fig-view-orig openInAnotherWindow btn js-view-large\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"/view-large/109886509\">\r\n          Open in new tab\r\n        </a></div></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">As exemplified in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig5\" data-open=\"fig5\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">5</a>, models with different shear/ellipticity result in different Einstein ring shapes (see also Kochanek, Keeton &amp; McLeod <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib20\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib20\" data-open=\"bib20\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2001</a>). Deeper and higher resolution imaging data would be useful to obtain a robust measurement of the lens ellipticity; and detect extended emission from the source host galaxy, thereby adding constraints to the lens model and breaking quadrupole degeneracies.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=109886511 id=\"109886511\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4-2>4.2 Peculiar false positives</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Some contaminants, such as single quasars and quasar-star alignments, are common in similar searches, like the SQLS (Oguri et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib27\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib27\" data-open=\"bib27\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>; Inada et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib18\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib18\" data-open=\"bib18\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>). Others, such as narrow-line galaxies (NLGs) at <em>z</em> \u2248 0.2\u20130.3 and star\u2013star alignments, are due to the lack of spectroscopic or UV-excess pre-selection. Some (cf. Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig6\" data-open=\"fig6\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">6</a>) deserve a special mention. A1507-1442 was flagged as a \u2018sure lens\u2019 because visual inspection showed a red galaxy between the two blue point-sources with identical colours identified automatically by cutout modelling, which however the ALFOSC data identified as stars. It had <span class=\"monospace\">ufom</span>=0.76; its UVx <em>u</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>g</em>\u00a0=\u00a0+0.49 (not entering the definition of <span class=\"monospace\">ufom</span>) was \u22481\u2009mag redder than the threshold \u22120.5 adopted used by Schechter et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib35\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib35\" data-open=\"bib35\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>). In general, this could also indicate a source at <em>z<sub>s</sub></em> \u2273 2, but this was not the case here. Similar considerations hold for A2243-3840 (<span class=\"monospace\">ufom</span>=0.56, <em>u</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>g</em>\u00a0=\u00a0\u22120.44). A2338-2700 shows two blue clumps on either side of a \u2018yellow\u2019 galaxy, whose NTT spectra have one secure line (possibly Mg <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a00.69) and no information on the central galaxy; preliminary imaging data (SOAR-SAM, PI Motta; not shown here) suggest that this system is probably a merger of NLGs, rather than a low-redshift lens. Spectra of A0054-3951 can be clearly de-blended, yielding a galaxy at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a00.475 (Mg\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>, O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>, H\u2009\u03b2) or a quasar at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.16 (C\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>], Ne\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">v</span>, [Ne\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span>]), plus a heavily reddened companion. Finally, the nature of A0008-3655 is unclear, as the lines in the fainter object may just be imperfections in the spectral de-convolution.</p>                        <a id=\"109886513\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx3226fig6.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Spectra of A1020 (<em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a02.03, top left), A0008 (top right), A2338 (bottom left), and A0054 (bottom right).</p></div></div>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=109886514 id=\"109886514\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4-3>4.3 Further candidates from a search in <em>Gaia</em>, and three additional lenses</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Further development can be brought by the high spatial resolution of <em>Gaia</em> (Lindegren et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib21\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib21\" data-open=\"bib21\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>), where Finet, Elyiv &amp; Surdej (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib15\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib15\" data-open=\"bib15\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>) estimated 0.06/deg<sup>2</sup> lensed quasars to be found within a limiting magnitude <em>G</em>\u00a0=\u00a020. In fact, in the current <em>Gaia</em>-DR1, about <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$20\\text{--}30 \\, {\\rm per \\, cent}$|</span> of known quasar lenses and pairs are recognized as multiple sources with separations \u2272 8\u2009arcsec, suggesting that these systems can be found by selecting quasar-like objects in WISE and then retaining those that correspond to <em>Gaia</em> multiplets. The details of this search are discussed elsewhere (Agnello <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>). When applied to objects with a counterpart in the public ATLAS footprint (i.e. covered in at least one band in DR3), this search recognized three known lenses (LBQS1009\u22120252, RXJ1131\u22121231, and W2329\u22121258: Hewett et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib17\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib17\" data-open=\"bib17\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1994</a>; Sluse et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib38\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib38\" data-open=\"bib38\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2003</a>; Schechter et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib35\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib35\" data-open=\"bib35\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>). A fourth lens, HE1113\u22120641 (Blackburne, Wisotzki &amp; Schechter <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib6\" data-open=\"bib6\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>, at 11<sup><em>h</em></sup>16<sup><em>m</em></sup>\u201306<sup><em>d</em></sup>57<sup><em>m</em></sup> in J2000 system), was re-discovered through the target selection of Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec2-1\"></span><a href=\"#sec2-1\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">2.1</a>, but due to its very small separation it is not resolved as a multiplet by <em>Gaia</em>-DR1.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">To facilitate follow-up, in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl4\" data-open=\"tbl4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a> we list additional candidates that could not be followed-up before this paper was completed, due to time and visibility constraints. Besides four identified in DR2 target+candidate selection and one found in DR3 with outlier selection (Agnello <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>), 11 (denoted by \u2018WGAhhmm-ddmm\u2019 names) are discovered purely from the <em>Gaia</em> multiplet search.<sup><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn3\" data-open=\"fn3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\">3</a></sup> Some of these were identified independently by the search of Schechter et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib35\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib35\" data-open=\"bib35\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>), using ATLAS cutout modelling of WISE-selected objects. Others, having ATLAS coverage in just two bands, could not be selected by the cutout modelling approach, but are found by the <em>Gaia</em> multiplet selection. Most of the candidates have Pan-STARRS1 <em>grizy</em> imaging, which we use to further grade them based on visual inspection.</p>                        <a id=\"109886517\" scrollto-destination=\"109886517\"></a>\r\n<div content-id=\"tbl4\" class=\"table-modal table-full-width-wrap\"><div class=\"table-wrap table-wide\"><div class=\"table-wrap-title\" id=\"tbl4\" data-id=\"tbl4\"><span class=\"label\">Table 4.</span><div class=\"caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Selected ATLAS-DR3 candidates, identified with various techniques, not followed up during the 2016 campaigns. The upper part of the table collects objects selected as in the previous sections; the middle part lists candidates selected among WISE-<em>Gaia</em> multiplets. <sup>(<em>a</em>)</sup> Some of these had also been flagged independently, through cutout modelling of the full footprint (Schechter et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib35\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib35\" data-open=\"bib35\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>). <sup>(<em>c</em>)</sup> Pan-STARRS1 <em>grizY</em> visual inspection excludes some systems with partial ATLAS-DR3 coverage. <sup>(<em>d</em>)</sup> After this paper was completed, independent campaigns in 2017 (NTT, PI Anguita; and WHT, Lemon et\u00a0al., private communication and in preparation) have targeted some of the systems in this table. Three are confirmed as NIQs in the spectra, and show a red excess in ATLAS and DES images (shown by Agnello et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4\" data-open=\"bib4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>), confirming them as additional lenses.</p></div> </div><div class=\"table-overflow\"><table><thead><tr><th>Name<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th>RA (J2000)<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th>Dec. S/N<sup>(<em>d</em>)</sup>\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>WGA1216\u22121138<sup>(<em>c</em>)</sup>\u00a0</td><td>184.130\u2009790\u00a0</td><td>\u221211.644\u2009588\u00a0</td><td>18.29\u00a0</td><td>\u2014\u00a0</td><td>\u2014\u00a0</td><td>DR3+<em>Gaia</em>\u00a0</td><td>Contaminant\u00a0</td><td>\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>WGA1112\u22121855<sup>(<em>c</em>)</sup>\u00a0</td><td>168.222\u2009452\u00a0</td><td>\u221218.916\u2009569\u00a0</td><td>19.39\u00a0</td><td>\u2014\u00a0</td><td>\u2014\u00a0</td><td>DR3+<em>Gaia</em>\u00a0</td><td>Contaminant\u00a0</td><td>\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>WGA1409\u22121444<sup>(<em>c</em>)</sup>\u00a0</td><td>212.250\u20092123\u00a0</td><td>\u221214.733\u2009644\u00a0</td><td>17.77\u00a0</td><td>\u2014\u00a0</td><td>\u2014\u00a0</td><td>DR3+<em>Gaia</em>\u00a0</td><td>Contaminant\u00a0</td><td>\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>A1201\u22120324<sup>(<em>c</em>)</sup>\u00a0</td><td>180.267\u2009310\u00a0</td><td>\u22123.402\u2009352\u00a0</td><td>19.10\u00a0</td><td>2.45\u00a0</td><td>0.15\u00a0</td><td>DR1+2\u00a0</td><td>Contaminant\u00a0</td><td>\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>A1333\u22120453<sup>(<em>c</em>)</sup>\u00a0</td><td>203.261\u2009960\u00a0</td><td>\u22124.898\u2009214\u00a0</td><td>19.41\u00a0</td><td>2.34\u00a0</td><td>0.19\u00a0</td><td>DR1+2\u00a0</td><td>Contaminant\u00a0</td><td>\u00a0</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class=\"&#xA;          graphic-wrap&#xA;          \"><a class=\"fig-view-orig openInAnotherWindow btn js-view-large\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"/view-large/109886517\">\r\n          Open in new tab\r\n        </a></div></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">After this paper was completed with the 2016 campaign results, three candidates of Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl4\" data-open=\"tbl4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a> (WGA0235\u22122433, WGA0259\u22122338, WGA0146\u22121133) were spectroscopically confirmed as lenses/NIQs in the fall of 2017, by two independent campaigns (NTT, PI Anguita; and WHT, Lemon et\u00a0al., private communication). These also fall in the DES footprint, where deeper <em>grizY</em> imaging in good seeing conditions shows red galaxies between the pairs of blue images (Agnello et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4\" data-open=\"bib4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>). As the discussion in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec4-1-2\"></span><a href=\"#sec4-1-2\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">4.1.2</a> and by Agnello et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4\" data-open=\"bib4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>) demonstrates, lens models on the discovery images are limited to \u2248 10\u2009per\u2009cent on the Einstein radii, due to systematics from the quadrupole contributions of shear and ellipticity. Besides that, in order to translate Einstein radii into masses, the redshifts of deflectors are needed. For these three systems, the data collected in 2017 are not deep enough to obtain a deflector redshift.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=109886519 id=\"109886519\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec5>5 SUMMARY AND PROSPECTS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">A rare-object search, charting the VST-ATLAS public footprint for lensed quasars, has yielded a new sample of NIQs, including previously unknown quasar lenses, out of a sample of 27 objects observed in 2016. The number of NIQs among followed-up systems could be higher, as two objects are confirmed quasars but currently inconclusive and three additional lenses (Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl4\" data-open=\"tbl4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a>) have been confirmed as NIQs/lenses in 2017 (PI Anguita, in preparation) after this paper was completed. This experiment demonstrated that previous searches (e.g. the SQLS, Oguri et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib27\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib27\" data-open=\"bib27\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>; Inada et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib18\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib18\" data-open=\"bib18\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>; More et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib22\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib22\" data-open=\"bib22\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>) can be extended to the regime of patchy waveband coverage and absence of <em>u</em>-band or spectroscopic pre-selection, still with moderate (\u22481\u2009arcsec) seeing and depth (\u224821 in <em>i</em> band). Due to the heterogeneous quality of survey data and range of expected image separations, a combination of techniques (Morgan et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib23\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib23\" data-open=\"bib23\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2004</a>; Ofek et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib25\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib25\" data-open=\"bib25\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2007</a>; Agnello et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib2\" data-open=\"bib2\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015a</a>; Agnello <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>, and Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec2\"></span><a href=\"#sec2\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">2</a> above) has been deployed. In all, the 2016 campaign and independent follow-up in 2017 (PI Anguita, PI Treu) have yielded five new quasar lenses and six NIQs.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The model-based candidate selection (applied to ATLAS-DR2) seems to give results comparable to the outlier-based target selection (applied to DR3), but is a necessary step to ascertain that the detected point sources have compatible colours and in fact it found lenses (Schechter et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib35\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib35\" data-open=\"bib35\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>) that were not flagged by the target selection. On the other hand, two systems (A1012-0307, A1020-1002) were identified via target selection, whereas independent cutout modelling had excluded them. While the lenses discovered in previous campaigns seem biased towards the colours of nearby quasars (see Williams, Agnello &amp; Treu <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib46\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib46\" data-open=\"bib46\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>, for a discussion), the ones selected here occupy distinctive regions of optical/IR colour\u2013magnitude diagrams (Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>), including sources at redshift <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0&gt;\u00a02.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=109886522 id=\"109886522\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec5-1>5.1 Spectral classification of pairs/NIQs and contaminants</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The primary aim of this search was to assemble a comprehensive sample of lenses/NIQs over the ATLAS (publicly accessible, DR3) footprint. From a sample of \u224810<sup>5</sup> objects with varying amount of multiband information, over<sup><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn4\" data-open=\"fn4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\">4</a></sup> \u22483000\u2009deg<sup>2</sup> and mostly brighter than <em>i</em>\u00a0=\u00a020, a sample of \u224840 objects was isolated for follow-up spectroscopy (Tables <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl3\" data-open=\"tbl3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a> and <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl4\" data-open=\"tbl4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a>). Given these final numbers, the spectra of all candidates can be visually inspected with ease, the most obvious contaminants excluded, and pairs/NIQs or lenses can be examined individually.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Upcoming spectroscopic surveys will render this task less immediate. For example, <em>Gaia</em>-DR4 is expected to provide low-resolution optical spectra of all detected sources (down to <em>G</em> \u2248 21, roughly <em>i</em> \u2248 23), over the whole sky, and the Euclid Wide survey (due 2021\u20132027) will obtain NIR slitless spectroscopy of objects down to <em>YJH</em> \u2248 24 over 15\u2009000\u2009deg<sup>2</sup>. If our ATLAS search is to be rescaled to these expectations, the number of spectra to be examined increases significantly and objective criteria should be devised to discard as many contaminants as possible, while also ensuring a complete selection, and retaining a \u2018manageable\u2019 sample for further inspection.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Learning from the sample presented in this paper, the following guidelines can be devised for objective (possibly semi-automatic) spectral classification of candidates. Since we are tasked with classification of spectra, a zeroth-order criterion would be the detection of the same (possibly broad) emission lines in both objects, at the same redshifts <em>z</em><sub>s</sub> \u2273 0.5, within a \u03b4<em>z</em> \u2248 0.005 measurement accuracy. This immediately eliminates chance alignments of different objects, and red galaxies seen between blue stars. A first criterion is given two spectra of putative multiple images, can they be fit as a common source spectrum with extinction/microlensing effects? Based on the spectra shown above, this translates into a model spectrum and a prescription for flux ratios and chromatic effects. The flux-ratio laws explored in this paper are either simple constants, in two wavelength ranges, or power-laws to imitate differential extinction. In order to account for the presence of a possible lens, which can contribute on the redder side of the spectra, the goodness-of-fit can be parametrized by two \u03c7<sup>2</sup> values, one from a model fit below \u03bb \u2272 5500\u2009\u212b (where the most prominent emission lines lie, typically), and one fit to \u03bb \u2273 6000\u2009\u212b. A second criterion is a refinement of the first are the flux ratios consistent among different lines, or among different ranges on the continua? This would then amount to three \u03c7<sup>2</sup> values overall: one for the continuum-subtracted lines, one on the continua below \u03bb \u2272 5500\u2009\u212b, and one for \u03bb \u2273 6000\u2009\u212b. The combination of these three criteria, accounting for 10\u201320\u2009per\u2009cent discrepancies in the flux ratios over lines and continua in different wavelength ranges, excludes all of the contaminants shown in this paper and retains all of the pairs/NIQs/lenses. Allowing for chromatic effects is important in order not to lose veritable lenses (e.g. LBQS1009\u22120252), and recognize possible lenses whose deflectors contribute to the spectra but are not bright enough to be resolved as separate spectral traces. In presence of spectra with good S/N, one can add a third criterion to classify objects as pairs or NIQs/lenses, by requiring that (once continuum-subtracted) the dispersions on corresponding lines are comparable across the multiple-image spectra. Requiring that the spectra contain broad lines at <em>z</em> \u2273 0.5 and with comparable dispersions (<em>not</em> simply the equivalent widths) eliminates most contaminants in the form of binary NLGs and binary quasars.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The criteria listed above can be translated into spectral grades, each corresponding roughly to the likelihood of realizing a NIQ/lens. The use of model \u03c7<sup>2</sup> values provides a smooth grading, and uncertainties in the observed spectra can be translated into data-driven uncertainties in the grades. This procedure in turn enables a quantitative (possibly automatic) evaluation of spectra, while also allowing for some flexibility in candidate ranking. A smooth, data-driven ranking scheme, which also incorporates uncertainties and is based on spectroscopic rather than broad-band information, can be tested on data from different campaigns. Scaling to larger samples, the spectra provided by <em>Gaia</em>-DR4 can be used as a testbed on large data sets, in view of automated and spectroscopic lens searches by the Euclid mission.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=109886527 id=\"109886527\" class=\"backacknowledgements-title\" >Acknowledgements</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The data presented here were obtained in part with ALFOSC, which is provided by the Instituto de Astrofisica de Andalucia (IAA) under a joint agreement with the University of Copenhagen and NOTSA.
