class=\"&#xA;          graphic-wrap&#xA;          \"><a class=\"fig-view-orig openInAnotherWindow btn js-view-large\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"/view-large/109886517\">\r\n          Open in new tab\r\n        </a></div></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">After this paper was completed with the 2016 campaign results, three candidates of Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl4\" data-open=\"tbl4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a> (WGA0235\u22122433, WGA0259\u22122338, WGA0146\u22121133) were spectroscopically confirmed as lenses/NIQs in the fall of 2017, by two independent campaigns (NTT, PI Anguita; and WHT, Lemon et\u00a0al., private communication). These also fall in the DES footprint, where deeper <em>grizY</em> imaging in good seeing conditions shows red galaxies between the pairs of blue images (Agnello et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4\" data-open=\"bib4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>). As the discussion in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec4-1-2\"></span><a href=\"#sec4-1-2\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">4.1.2</a> and by Agnello et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4\" data-open=\"bib4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>) demonstrates, lens models on the discovery images are limited to \u2248 10\u2009per\u2009cent on the Einstein radii, due to systematics from the quadrupole contributions of shear and ellipticity. Besides that, in order to translate Einstein radii into masses, the redshifts of deflectors are needed. For these three systems, the data collected in 2017 are not deep enough to obtain a deflector redshift.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=109886519 id=\"109886519\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec5>5 SUMMARY AND PROSPECTS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">A rare-object search, charting the VST-ATLAS public footprint for lensed quasars, has yielded a new sample of NIQs, including previously unknown quasar lenses, out of a sample of 27 objects observed in 2016. The number of NIQs among followed-up systems could be higher, as two objects are confirmed quasars but currently inconclusive and three additional lenses (Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl4\" data-open=\"tbl4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a>) have been confirmed as NIQs/lenses in 2017 (PI Anguita, in preparation) after this paper was completed. This experiment demonstrated that previous searches (e.g. the SQLS, Oguri et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib27\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib27\" data-open=\"bib27\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>; Inada et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib18\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib18\" data-open=\"bib18\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>; More et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib22\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib22\" data-open=\"bib22\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>) can be extended to the regime of patchy waveband coverage and absence of <em>u</em>-band or spectroscopic pre-selection, still with moderate (\u22481\u2009arcsec) seeing and depth (\u224821 in <em>i</em> band). Due to the heterogeneous quality of survey data and range of expected image separations, a combination of techniques (Morgan et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib23\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib23\" data-open=\"bib23\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2004</a>; Ofek et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib25\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib25\" data-open=\"bib25\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2007</a>; Agnello et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib2\" data-open=\"bib2\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015a</a>; Agnello <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>, and Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec2\"></span><a href=\"#sec2\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">2</a> above) has been deployed. In all, the 2016 campaign and independent follow-up in 2017 (PI Anguita, PI Treu) have yielded five new quasar lenses and six NIQs.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The model-based candidate selection (applied to ATLAS-DR2) seems to give results comparable to the outlier-based target selection (applied to DR3), but is a necessary step to ascertain that the detected point sources have compatible colours and in fact it found lenses (Schechter et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib35\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib35\" data-open=\"bib35\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>) that were not flagged by the target selection. On the other hand, two systems (A1012-0307, A1020-1002) were identified via target selection, whereas independent cutout modelling had excluded them. While the lenses discovered in previous campaigns seem biased towards the colours of nearby quasars (see Williams, Agnello &amp; Treu <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib46\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib46\" data-open=\"bib46\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>, for a discussion), the ones selected here occupy distinctive regions of optical/IR colour\u2013magnitude diagrams (Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>), including sources at redshift <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0&gt;\u00a02.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=109886522 id=\"109886522\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec5-1>5.1 Spectral classification of pairs/NIQs and contaminants</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The primary aim of this search was to assemble a comprehensive sample of lenses/NIQs over the ATLAS (publicly accessible, DR3) footprint. From a sample of \u224810<sup>5</sup> objects with varying amount of multiband information, over<sup><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn4\" data-open=\"fn4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\">4</a></sup> \u22483000\u2009deg<sup>2</sup> and mostly brighter than <em>i</em>\u00a0=\u00a020, a sample of \u224840 objects was isolated for follow-up spectroscopy (Tables <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl3\" data-open=\"tbl3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a> and <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl4\" data-open=\"tbl4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a>). Given these final numbers, the spectra of all candidates can be visually inspected with ease, the most obvious contaminants excluded, and pairs/NIQs or lenses can be examined individually.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Upcoming spectroscopic surveys will render this task less immediate. For example, <em>Gaia</em>-DR4 is expected to provide low-resolution optical spectra of all detected sources (down to <em>G</em> \u2248 21, roughly <em>i</em> \u2248 23), over the whole sky, and the Euclid Wide survey (due 2021\u20132027) will obtain NIR slitless spectroscopy of objects down to <em>YJH</em> \u2248 24 over 15\u2009000\u2009deg<sup>2</sup>. If our ATLAS search is to be rescaled to these expectations, the number of spectra to be examined increases significantly and objective criteria should be devised to discard as many contaminants as possible, while also ensuring a complete selection, and retaining a \u2018manageable\u2019 sample for further inspection.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Learning from the sample presented in this paper, the following guidelines can be devised for objective (possibly semi-automatic) spectral classification of candidates. Since we are tasked with classification of spectra, a zeroth-order criterion would be the detection of the same (possibly broad) emission lines in both objects, at the same redshifts <em>z</em><sub>s</sub> \u2273 0.5, within a \u03b4<em>z</em> \u2248 0.005 measurement accuracy. This immediately eliminates chance alignments of different objects, and red galaxies seen between blue stars. A first criterion is given two spectra of putative multiple images, can they be fit as a common source spectrum with extinction/microlensing effects? Based on the spectra shown above, this translates into a model spectrum and a prescription for flux ratios and chromatic effects. The flux-ratio laws explored in this paper are either simple constants, in two wavelength ranges, or power-laws to imitate differential extinction. In order to account for the presence of a possible lens, which can contribute on the redder side of the spectra, the goodness-of-fit can be parametrized by two \u03c7<sup>2</sup> values, one from a model fit below \u03bb \u2272 5500\u2009\u212b (where the most prominent emission lines lie, typically), and one fit to \u03bb \u2273 6000\u2009\u212b. A second criterion is a refinement of the first are the flux ratios consistent among different lines, or among different ranges on the continua? This would then amount to three \u03c7<sup>2</sup> values overall: one for the continuum-subtracted lines, one on the continua below \u03bb \u2272 5500\u2009\u212b, and one for \u03bb \u2273 6000\u2009\u212b. The combination of these three criteria, accounting for 10\u201320\u2009per\u2009cent discrepancies in the flux ratios over lines and continua in different wavelength ranges, excludes all of the contaminants shown in this paper and retains all of the pairs/NIQs/lenses. Allowing for chromatic effects is important in order not to lose veritable lenses (e.g. LBQS1009\u22120252), and recognize possible lenses whose deflectors contribute to the spectra but are not bright enough to be resolved as separate spectral traces. In presence of spectra with good S/N, one can add a third criterion to classify objects as pairs or NIQs/lenses, by requiring that (once continuum-subtracted) the dispersions on corresponding lines are comparable across the multiple-image spectra. Requiring that the spectra contain broad lines at <em>z</em> \u2273 0.5 and with comparable dispersions (<em>not</em> simply the equivalent widths) eliminates most contaminants in the form of binary NLGs and binary quasars.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The criteria listed above can be translated into spectral grades, each corresponding roughly to the likelihood of realizing a NIQ/lens. The use of model \u03c7<sup>2</sup> values provides a smooth grading, and uncertainties in the observed spectra can be translated into data-driven uncertainties in the grades. This procedure in turn enables a quantitative (possibly automatic) evaluation of spectra, while also allowing for some flexibility in candidate ranking. A smooth, data-driven ranking scheme, which also incorporates uncertainties and is based on spectroscopic rather than broad-band information, can be tested on data from different campaigns. Scaling to larger samples, the spectra provided by <em>Gaia</em>-DR4 can be used as a testbed on large data sets, in view of automated and spectroscopic lens searches by the Euclid mission.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=109886527 id=\"109886527\" class=\"backacknowledgements-title\" >Acknowledgements</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The data presented here were obtained in part with ALFOSC, which is provided by the Instituto de Astrofisica de Andalucia (IAA) under a joint agreement with the University of Copenhagen and NOTSA. class=\"end-note-link\">4</span></span><div class=\"footnote-content\"><p class=\"footnote-compatibility\">This is an estimate of the effective footprint, which accounts for inhomogeneous waveband coverage of the DR3 footprint as of 2016, when the searches were performed.</p></div></span></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=109886537 id=\"109886537\" class=\"backreferences-title\" R.</div></span> et al.\u00a0</span>, <div class=\"year\">2017b</div>, <div class=\"comment\">preprint (<a class=\"link link-uri openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"http://arxiv.org/abs/1706.01506\" target=\"_blank\">arXiv:1706.01506</a>)</div></p></div></div></div></div><div content-id=\"bib48\" data-legacy-id=\"bib48\"><div class=\"refLink-parent\"><span class=\"refLink\"><a name=\"jumplink-bib48\" href=\"javascript:;\" aria-label=\"jumplink-bib48\"></a></span></div><div class=\"ref false\"><div id=\"ref-auto-bib48\" class=\"ref-content \"><div class=\"mixed-citation citation\"><p class=\"mixed-citation-compatibility\">\r\n<span class=\"person-group\"><span class=\"name string-name\"><div class=\"surname\">Wisotzki</div>  <div class=\"given-names\">L.</div></span>, <span class=\"name string-name\"><div class=\"surname\">Koehler</div>  <div class=\"given-names\">T.</div></span>, <span class=\"name string-name\"><div class=\"surname\">Kayser</div>  <div class=\"given-names\">R.</div></span>, <span class=\"name string-name\"><div class=\"surname\">Reimers</div>  <div class=\"given-names\">D.</div></span></span>, <div class=\"year\">1993</div>, <div class=\"source \">A&amp;A</div>, <div class=\"volume\">278</div>, <div class=\"fpage\">L15</div></p><!--citationLinks: case 2--><div class=\"citation-links\">\u00a0</div></div></div></div></div><div content-id=\"bib49\" data-legacy-id=\"bib49\"><div class=\"refLink-parent\"><span class=\"refLink\"><a name=\"jumplink-bib49\" href=\"javascript:;\" aria-label=\"jumplink-bib49\"></a></span></div><div class=\"ref false\"><div id=\"ref-auto-bib49\" class=\"ref-content \"><div class=\"mixed-citation citation\"><p class=\"mixed-citation-compatibility\">\r\n<span class=\"person-group\"><span class=\"name string-name\"><div class=\"surname\">Wright</div>  <div class=\"given-names\">E. L.</div></span> et al.\u00a0</span>, <div class=\"year\">2010</div>, <div class=\"source \">AJ</div>, <div class=\"volume\">140</div>, <div class=\"fpage\">1868</div></p><!--citationLinks: case 1--><div class=\"citation-links\"></div><div class=\"citation-links\"><div class=\"crossref-doi js-ref-link\"><a class=\"openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"http://dx.doi.org/10.1088/0004-6256/140/6/1868\" target=\"_blank\">Crossref</a></div><div class=\"adsDoiReference\"><a class=\"openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/cgi-bin/basic_connect?qsearch=10.1088%2F0004-6256%2F140%2F6%2F1868\" target=\"_blank\">Search ADS</a></div><div class=\"xslopenurl empty-target\"><span class=\"inst-open-url-holders\" data-targetId=\"10.1088%2F0004-6256%2F140%2F6%2F1868\"> </span></div>\u00a0</div></div></div></div></div><div content-id=\"bib50\" data-legacy-id=\"bib50\"><div class=\"refLink-parent\"><span class=\"refLink\"><a name=\"jumplink-bib50\" href=\"javascript:;\" aria-label=\"jumplink-bib50\"></a></span></div><div class=\"ref false\"><div id=\"ref-auto-bib50\" class=\"ref-content \"><div class=\"mixed-citation citation\"><p class=\"mixed-citation-compatibility\">\r\n<span class=\"person-group\"><span class=\"name string-name\"><div class=\"surname\">Zahedy</div>  <div class=\"given-names\">F. S.</div></span>, <span class=\"name string-name\"><div class=\"surname\">Chen</div>  <div class=\"given-names\">H.-W.</div></span>, <span class=\"name string-name\"><div class=\"surname\">Rauch</div>  <div class=\"given-names\">M.</div></span>, <span class=\"name string-name\"><div class=\"surname\">Wilson</div>  <div class=\"given-names\">M. L.</div></span>, <span class=\"name string-name\"><div class=\"surname\">Zabludoff</div>  <div class=\"given-names\">A.</div></span></span>, <div class=\"year\">2016</div>, <div class=\"source \">MNRAS</div>, <div class=\"volume\">458</div>, <div class=\"fpage\">2423</div></p><!--citationLinks: case 1--><div class=\"citation-links\"></div><div class=\"citation-links\"><div class=\"crossref-doi js-ref-link\"><a class=\"openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"http://dx.doi.org/10.1093/mnras/stw484\" target=\"_blank\">Crossref</a></div><div class=\"adsDoiReference\"><a class=\"openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/cgi-bin/basic_connect?qsearch=10.1093%2Fmnras%2Fstw484\" target=\"_blank\">Search ADS</a></div><div class=\"xslopenurl empty-target\"><span class=\"inst-open-url-holders\" data-targetId=\"10.1093%2Fmnras%2Fstw484\"> </span></div>\u00a0</div></div></div></div></div></div>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=109886539 id=\"109886539\" class=\"appendix-title\" data-legacy-id=sec6>APPENDIX: THE \u2018LOCUS\u2019 OF SIE + XS SOLUTIONS FOR A0140-1152</h3>\r\n<div class=\"&#xA;            block-child-p&#xA;            \">A model with SIE and external shear, when fit to the image configuration and flux ratios of a double, is unconstrained. Here, we explore the main degeneracies among parameters that result in the same observed constraints. In what follows, we fix the lens p.a. to that measured from the cutouts, i.e. 28\u2009deg E of N, with an uncertainty of 5\u2009deg. Besides the measurements (image positions, flux ratios), an additional constraint is the presence of only two observed images; this splits the parameter space into different connected components, possibly more than two, i.e. there may be two (separate) connected components within which two images are produced. These connected components are not compact, since there are sequence of parameter choices that converge to solutions where neither two nor four (non-degenerate) images are produced. The \u2018locus\u2019 is the set of points (parameter choices) for which two images are produced and the measured constraints are satisfied. The projection of the \u2018locus\u2019 on different parameters is non-trivial; for example, the Einstein radius is \u22480.73\u2009arcsec for most values of the axial ratio, increasing towards \u22480.8\u2009arcsec when <em>q</em> approaches 0.35 (\u03b3<sub>s</sub> \u2248 0.216). This explains why \u03b8<sub>E</sub> \u2248 0.73\u2009arcsec is robust against the chosen model (\u2018a\u2019 or \u2018b\u2019 in the main text), unless one posits significant ellipticity in the lens. When <em>q</em>\u00a0&gt;\u00a00.9, the shear is small (\u03b3<sub>s</sub>\u00a0&lt;\u00a00.02) and the solutions are almost independent of it. Within 0.5 \u2272 <em>q</em> \u2272 0.9, there is a simple relation between shear amplitude and flattening: <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equa1\" content-id=\"equa1\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{equation}\r\n\\gamma _{\\text{s}} \\approx -0.39(q - 1.0) - 0.018\\ ,\r\n\\end{equation} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(A1)</span></div>slightly steeper (resp. shallower) at lower (resp. higher) <em>q</em>. At shear values above 0.02, the \u2018locus\u2019 projects almost orthogonally on the shear angle, i.e. \u03d5<sub>s</sub> \u2248 60\u2009deg almost independently of the shear amplitude. This is just because shear and ellipticity must compensate to yield a small quadrupole (to produce only two images), and the lens p.a. is kept fixed (within 5\u00a0deg tolerance). These relations are shown in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-figa1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"figa1\" data-open=\"figa1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">A1</a>. Since the \u2018locus\u2019 is topologically non-trivial, we explored a tube around it, adopting small but finite uncertainties on the constraints. The non-compactness of the locus can be understood as \u03b3<sub>s</sub> does not approach the same value as \u03c6<sub>s</sub> approaches \u224860\u2009deg from the right or from the left. The plots are truncated at \u03b3<sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.1, just for visual convenience. The shear and flattening \u2018saturate\u2019 towards \u03b3 \u2248 0.05 and <em>q</em> \u2248 0.96. This also explains the parameters inferred for the restricted models (a, b) in the main text.</div>                        <a id=\"109886541\" scrollto-destination=\"109886541\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"figa1\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure A1.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/475/2/10.1093_mnras_stx3226/1/m_stx3226figa1.jpeg?Expires=1611466225&amp;Signature=V80x8WM1Gr4Ve28NSOupj5lJYDmQ2eGjfJvPzU35c0qp25o-5fcuwRpQG8P1LPmjiWNS~W7Kcvq4l8X4Jzqn7nFdLoQibL8kOsiGKCreKQGRyqwmx8d1rxnyj9tygjClEuWTQOY1CQRDvezfdQ6-Egp9ysXd0Gj1PyNEeCaNjdSFV8UOg2nFERSn~jNvQfot5cSEDmjdBklJMmU6VBamaGsmukx-Wr6TBx9DLBIXQ2aJd5CGDAQ2QoLfpm61jCoyF7WqiDEzj9PsbHTTVgnEMbFF3EjXwsQU06il~LfUW2kWG9ZiuUf~7Nm~cbBCAwOwBU4xUKRiVYCkF8z3qmHP3Q__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Degeneracies between parameters in mod.(c, SIE+XS), with small uncertainties on the measured constraints in order to explore a \u2018tube\u2019 of general solutions. The lens model parameters are sampled uniformly, except for the lens p.a., which is constrained to its measured value within 5\u2009deg.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx3226figa1.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/109886541/stx3226figa1.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx3226figa1.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"109886541\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/475/2/10.1093_mnras_stx3226/1/stx3226figa1.jpeg?Expires=1611466225&Signature=K2h24elTFzH1i8gGlpKSk5jgombfJd7Y9Es9qXSgo-E8iB2kYt7Njgyz~ZjkzvrReeFI7wM17LJwM9mmLLoPLLdYUV4AVAoxXoduUoVx0TW51RfRGWWmsMoAMTWY0-TL0WyjO2MFOpomMbYm5G3g~B~7FIwo~Vn7-vAJCaA8UtY3wufq07LPgLlGCa-eBWAzKQ15OPkWB~GUfHkgyqmCx5K5FFwJRUbJdnkRL3Dec8HWs-h8l4U6QPSZZSfSJ9y7SbozAF1GEx2dRNOXRbbArwg6N5hK7Io1XeMseNT82udsx5oQaOLf7euhlunMBX-lJ4pMuxSITwGyJlG1WTp0uA__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=109886541&ar=4739362&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx3226figa1.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Degeneracies between parameters in mod.(c, SIE+XS), with small uncertainties on the measured constraints in order to explore a \u2018tube\u2019 of general solutions. Gran Breta\u00f1a 1111, Playa Ancha, Valparaso 2360102, Chile), AL(Department of Physics, Centre for Extragalactic Astronomy, Durham University, Durham DH1 3LE, England), AM(Department of Physics, Centre for Extragalactic Astronomy, Durham University, Durham DH1 3LE, England)"], "journal_name": "Monthly Notices of the Royal Astronomical Society", "volume": "475", "publication_year": "2018/04/1", "start_page": "2086", "end_page": "2096", "keywords": ["gravitational lensing: strong", "methods: statistical", "techniques: image processing", "surveys", "quasars: general", "Astrophysics - Cosmology and Nongalactic Astrophysics", "Astrophysics - Astrophysics of Galaxies"], "url": "https://ui.adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2018MNRAS.475.2086A", "abstract": "We report on discovery results from a quasar lens search in the ATLAS-DR3 public footprint. Spectroscopic follow-up campaigns, conducted at the 2.6 m Nordic Optical Telescope (La Palma) and 3.6 m New Technology Telescope (La Silla) in 2016, yielded seven pairs of quasars exhibiting the same lines at the same redshift and monotonic flux ratios with wavelength (hereafter NIQs, nearly identical quasar pairs). Magellan spectra of A0140-1152 (01<SUP>h</SUP>40<SUP>m</SUP>03{^s<SUB>.</SUB>}0-11<SUP>d</SUP>52<SUP>m</SUP>19{^s<SUB>.</SUB>}0, z<SUB>s</SUB> = 1.807) confirm it as a lens with deflector at z<SUB>l</SUB> = 0.277 and Einstein radius \u03b8<SUB>E</SUB> = (0.73 \u00b1 0.02) arcsec. Follow-up imaging of the NIQ A2213-2652 (22<SUP>h</SUP>13<SUP>m</SUP>38{^s<SUB>.</SUB>}4-26<SUP>d</SUP>52<SUP>m</SUP>27{^s<SUB>.</SUB>}1) reveals the deflector galaxy and confirms it as a lens. We show the use of spatial resolution from the Gaia mission to select lenses and list additional systems from a WISE-Gaia-ATLAS search, yielding three additional lenses (02<SUP>h</SUP>35<SUP>m</SUP>27{^s<SUB>.</SUB>}4-24<SUP>d</SUP>33<SUP>m</SUP>13{^s<SUB>.</SUB>}2, 02<SUP>h</SUP>59<SUP>m</SUP>33<SUP>s</SUP>-23<SUP>d</SUP>38<SUP>m</SUP>01{^s<SUB>.</SUB>}8, 01<SUP>h</SUP>46<SUP>m</SUP>32{^s<SUB>.</SUB>}9-11<SUP>d</SUP>33<SUP>m</SUP>39{^s<SUB>.</SUB>}0). The overall sample consists of 11 lenses/NIQs, plus three lenses known before 2016, over the ATLAS-DR3 footprint (\u22483500 deg<SUP>2</SUP>). Finally, we discuss future prospects for objective classification of pair/NIQ/contaminant spectra.", "doi": "10.1093/mnras/stx3226", "custom1": "eprint: arXiv:1711.07492", "issn": "0035-8711", "number": "2"}, "Inspection status": "Incomplete"}
